# Status

> The cross-tool handoff doc. **Read the "Now" block at the start of a session;
> update it (and prepend to the Log) at the end.** See `AGENTS.md` for the
> handoff protocol, `DECISIONS.md` for why, `ARCHITECTURE.md` for the spec.

## Now

**2026-07-18 — Batch 139 — Check-in edits survive a warm-resume refetch — BUILT + pushed for review (branch `fix/batch-139-checkin-refetch-clobber`); 🔴 High, Decision #218; closeout pending.** Triggered by Mark reporting his **check-in details "aren't being saved."** Investigated against prod data (`coach` schema): his 2026-07-18 morning `manual_entry` was created 09:05:49 with **every field null** and the brief generated 47 s later — so the PUT fired with an empty body — versus 11/12 Jul rows created-then-updated with his real values and 7 Jul's empty+full pair 8 s apart. **Root cause (frontend, no backend bug — `DailyLoopService.upsert_manual_entry`/`_manual_entry` are symmetric on `entry_date` and commit fine):** `CheckInPage.tsx`'s `useEffect([query.data])` (`:132`) re-seeds `manualForm` from the server's `manualEntry` on **every** `['daily-loop']` refetch, with no dirty-edit guard. On Mark's iOS PWA, `refetchOnWindowFocus` (`lib/queryClient.ts:22`) is widened to fire on `pageshow`/warm resume (`lib/resumeRefetch.ts`, `App.tsx:77`); a warm resume mid-check-in refetches, a fresh envelope's new `meta.generatedAtUtc` makes React Query's structural sharing hand back a **new `query.data` reference**, the effect re-runs and blanks his unsaved edits, then "Get today's brief" saves an empty entry. **Built (frontend-only, no API/shared-schema/migration):** a `dirtyRef` set by `setManual`/`toggleChip` (covering the feel buttons, quick chips, and every free-text/BP field) makes the seed effect early-return once he has edited; `saveMutation.onSuccess` clears it so the post-save invalidation re-seeds cleanly from the stored values; pristine seeding (first load / later backstop-generated entry) unchanged. Restores the "dirty-state-safe across a focus refetch" contract `resumeRefetch.ts:18` already assumed — `CheckInPage` was the sole exception. **Gates (local, green):** `CheckInPage.test.tsx` **10 passed** (2 new — a mid-edit refetch returning a distinct envelope preserves the typed score+chip and the save PUTs them not empties, *verified to fail without the guard*; a pristine form still adopts a server entry on a later refetch), web `tsc --noEmit` clean, eslint clean on touched files. Docs updated on-branch: `docs/phase-batches.md` (new Batch 139 section, unstruck/`In review`), `DECISIONS.md` #218. **Next:** poll GitHub CI to green, then `/closeout` (merge → prod-verify → strike the ledger row + set #218 as the durable record). **Follow-ups noted, deliberately *not* bundled:** (a) the empty-payload overwrite in `upsert_manual_entry` — an all-empty PUT still replaces a populated row (a backend guard would be defence-in-depth); (b) missing morning-entry uniqueness/locking, which produced 7 Jul's duplicate rows. Batch 138's own follow-ups remain open (duplicate iPhone push subs still both active; Mark's Android push row needs a live test-notification).

**2026-07-17 — Closed out Batch 138 — Daily-loop freshness, stale-cache fix & later 11:00 morning backstop — SHIPPED (PR #165, squash `f23078b`); production verified.** 🔴 High, Decision **#217**. Triggered by Craig reporting the PWA opening on **yesterday's** brief (same session that surfaced the double-notification — root-caused separately to two active iPhone push subscriptions, and a re-activation of Mark's dormant Android push row in prod). **Root cause of the stale brief (not a backend date bug — `daily_loop._local_today` correctly uses the profile timezone):** the service worker's `NetworkFirst` `/api/v1/daily-loop` route fell back to its ≤24h Workbox cache after only a **5 s** timeout, and Batch 62.1's `PersistQueryClientProvider` paints that last-good response instantly on cold launch — and a stale hit was **invisible** (no banner, no forced refetch). **Built (frontend, no API/schema change — the envelope already carries `subjectDate`):** (138.1) new `localTodayIso(timeZone)` in `lib/dailyFlow.ts` (`Intl.DateTimeFormat('en-CA',{timeZone})`, no date lib) = the same local-today the backend derives; `DashboardPage` compares it to `data.subjectDate` and, when online and they differ, renders a new `StaleDataNotice` (sibling to `OfflineNotice`, `role="status"`) "Showing {day}'s brief — refresh for today's" with a **Refresh** button. (138.2) `fetchDailyLoop(subjectDate,{forceFresh})` passes `cache:'reload'` so the refresh bypasses the HTTP cache and (NetworkFirst tries network first) forces a genuinely fresh read; SW `api-daily-loop` `networkTimeoutSeconds` **5 → 10**. (138.3) `WeekAheadPage.tsx`'s `todayIso` was `new Date().toISOString().slice(0,10)` (UTC date — rolls a day late during BST, can mis-highlight "today" at the ~23:00-UTC boundary) → now `localTodayIso(player?.timezone)`. **(138.4) Backstop retune (Craig: keep the guaranteed verdict, just move the deadline out):** `wake_detection.py` `BACKSTOP` **09:30→11:00**, `WINDOW_END` **10:00→11:30** (30 min past the backstop so `run_wake_check` is still polling when it fires); `morning_backstop` cron **09:30→11:00**. Cadence/`settle_min`/floor/stability-guard unchanged. The old 09:30 (Decision #87) hugged Mark's latest-observed wake (09:24); a genuine lie-in got force-read (`past_backstop→fire`) on stale data before he was up. Only lie-in / watch-not-worn days move (a normal morning wake-detects ~08:22 and never reaches the backstop) — and they still get a guaranteed verdict, just later. **Decisions settled with Craig at `/batch-start` (2026-07-17):** backstop **11:00** (of 10:30/11:00/10:00 offered); stale UI = **top notice + Refresh** (vs inline card); SW timeout = **10 s** (of 8/10/6). **Boundaries:** frontend + the backstop constant/cron-time change only; no API/shared-schema/migration; verdict/Green-Amber-Red/#133/#135/Red-never-VO2 untouched; `docs/designs/wake-triggered-morning.md` carries an as-built update note (historical 09:30 calibration preserved). **Gates (local):** backend pytest **634 passed / 227 skipped**, `ruff check`+`format --check` clean, `mypy src` clean (113 files); web `tsc --noEmit` clean, eslint clean on touched files; new tests — `dailyFlow.test.ts` (5), `DashboardPage.test.tsx` (+3), `WeekAheadPage.test.tsx` (+1), `test_wake_detection.py` (+1 & retuned), `test_scheduler.py` (backstop cron `hour='11'`); production build clean (Node 20, `✓ built in 26.59s`). **CI caught a real regression the local run masked:** the first `SleepPage.test.tsx` failure (`toHaveBeenCalledWith('/api/v1/daily-loop?subject_date=…')`) was **not** a cold-start timeout as first assumed — adding an `init` param to `fetchDailyLoop` had made the *normal* fetch call `apiFetch(path, undefined)` (two args), breaking single-arg call assertions; the local full run's contention noise (521s, concurrent build) hid it among genuine `userEvent` timeouts in untouched files (`HandoverPage`, `WeekAheadPage` move-picker). **Fix (amend `e3869e4`):** only the forced refresh passes an init (`cache: 'reload'`); the normal path stays `apiFetch(path)` single-arg. After that, both CI waves passed all 7 jobs + Vercel preview. **Merge:** squash `f23078b` (#165). **Production on `f23078b723bb9e20960ef0616c5130eff4c9ad41`:** Railway `/api/v1/health` + Vercel same-origin `/api/v1/health` both served that SHA; web `/` `200`; unauthenticated `/api/v1/daily-loop` `401` both direct and via the Vercel proxy. **Next:** no unshipped rows remain in `docs/phase-batches.md` — pick the next priority with Craig. Two follow-ups noted: the double-notification's duplicate iPhone push subscriptions (two active rows for the same device) are still both active and will keep doubling Mark→Craig's pushes until deactivated; and Mark's Android push row was re-activated in prod but needs a live "Send test notification" to confirm the endpoint is still valid. **Deferred live-use:** the on-device eyeball of the stale banner + refresh (needs a real stale cache) and the 11:00 backstop firing remain live-use verification — same live-browser constraint as prior batches ([[ui-walkthrough-method]]); covered by the deterministic unit tests meanwhile.

**2026-07-17 — Closed out Batch 137 — Premium UI/UX polish pass — SHIPPED (PR #164, squash `9e71731`); production verified.** 🟢 Mid, Decision **#216**. A frontend-only design-review polish pass (came from Craig asking for a final "most premium it can be" UI/UX review). The four open calls were settled with Craig at `/batch-start`: **SaveButton = async saves only; Skeleton = wire in the shimmer; toaster = reposition + tokenise; pinch-zoom = re-enable.** **Built:** (137.1) theme-aware recharts via new `lib/chartColors.ts` + `useChartColors()` — `TrendsPage` & `BedroomOvernightChart` no longer freeze to the dark palette on white in light mode (the `<Tooltip>` `var()` styling was already correct and stays). (137.2) `Textarea` → `text-base sm:text-sm` (kills the iOS focus-zoom), `PinInput` → shared `controlFieldClassName`. (137.3) `SaveButton` adopted at **Settings → Change PIN only** (see finding), with a new optional `icon` prop + `useSaveButtonState(isPending,isSuccess)` adapter (`hooks/useSaveButtonState.ts`). (137.4) `Skeleton` → `.animate-shimmer`; new `ScrollToTop` (resets on PUSH, no-ops on POP); `TabBar` active-underline `layoutId` spring gated on `useReducedMotion()`. (137.5) new `AppToaster` (bottom-centre, tab-bar-safe offset, in-app `theme`, token left-accent colours, `richColors` dropped) replacing the inline bottom-right Toaster; `index.html` viewport drops `maximum-scale/user-scalable=no`. **137.3 finding (recorded in #216):** the review assumed broad SaveButton adoption, but nearly every save in this app refetches and unmounts/switches its own button on success (Holiday pause→active card, Dashboard/Week confirm panels collapse, Check-in→generating view), so the Saved✓ can't show — it would flash then unmount; so it was applied only where the full lifecycle is visible (Change PIN) and the long-running/collapse/navigate buttons keep their spinner/label affordance. A uniform *pending* affordance on the rest is an offered follow-up. **Gate (local, green):** web `tsc --noEmit` clean; eslint 0 errors (6 known warnings); production build clean (Node 20); new tests — chartColors (2), save-button (3), useSaveButtonState (2), ScrollToTop (1), PinInput (1), skeleton (1), + a Textarea-16px case in `controls.test.tsx` — all pass; full web vitest passes warm (the 2 `WeekAheadPage` cold-start `userEvent` 5000ms timeouts are the pre-existing #122/#214 esbuild flakiness — a file this batch never touched, both pass in isolation in <1s). **Boundaries:** frontend-only; no API/shared-schema/migration; verdict/advisory/Green-Amber-Red/#133/#135/Red-never-VO2 untouched. **CI:** both branch-push and PR-context waves passed all 7 jobs (incl. `Unit tests (web + shared)`) plus the Vercel preview; the local full-suite `WeekAheadPage` cold-start timeouts did not recur in CI. **Production on merge SHA `9e717312aa0205346e656673945335210a87f723`:** Railway `/api/v1/health` served that SHA; web `/`, `/trends`, `/settings`, `/environment` returned `200` and the served viewport meta confirms the new build (no `user-scalable=no`); unauthenticated `/api/v1/daily-loop` returned `401` both direct and via the Vercel same-origin proxy. **Next:** no unshipped rows remain in `docs/phase-batches.md` — pick the next priority with Craig. Two open threads flagged at closeout: (a) whether to broaden 137.3 to a uniform *pending* affordance (consistent in-flight icon + "…") on the long-running/collapse buttons SaveButton doesn't fit; (b) a pre-existing `bg-surface-muted` no-op utility class in `PowerProfilePreview.tsx:56` (undefined token, likely from the Batch 135 extraction) worth a separate fix. **Deferred live-use:** on-device eyeball of the light-mode charts, the shimmer, the repositioned toasts, pinch-zoom, and the Change-PIN Saved✓ remains deferred — same live-browser constraint as prior batches ([[ui-walkthrough-method]]); covered by the unit tests meanwhile.

**2026-07-16 — Closed out Batch 135 — Tap a workout to open a detail sheet — SHIPPED (PR #162, squash `236dacb`); production verified.** 🟢 Mid, Decision **#214**. The Week view's workout rows were display-only dead ends (there is no workout-detail route anywhere in `App.tsx`); they are now tappable into a new read-only `WorkoutDetailSheet`. **Reuse over duplication:** the structured-ride blob parser + segment→bars expander and the power-profile SVG were extracted out of `StructuredWorkoutSheet` (Batch 88) into a shared `apps/web/src/lib/structuredWorkout.ts` + `apps/web/src/components/PowerProfilePreview.tsx`, which both the editor and the new sheet import — the editor keeps only its editor-specific validation/submit, and the shared parser is *faithful* (returns no segments for an unstructured session) with the warm-up→steady→cool-down starting template left in the editor, so a read-only surface can tell "has structure" from "none". The sheet shows title, discipline, status (Completed/Skipped/To do), planned duration, intensity target, indoor/outdoor + Garmin-delivery state, coach-planned-vs-you-added source, and — for a structured bike session — the interval breakdown + reused power-profile preview; other sessions get an honest "No structured breakdown for this session." line. Tap-to-open is wired on **both** the read-first glance (`GlanceDayRow`, Mark's surface, whole row → button) and the admin editor rows (`WorkoutRow`, title/summary → button, leaving Move / Edit structure / Skip / Remove untouched and un-nested); the unplanned-activity chips (Batch 133) stay non-interactive; the sheet never edits. **Boundaries:** frontend + shared-module refactor only; no API/shared-schema/migration; Green/Amber/Red, #133, #135, Red-never-VO2 untouched. **Gates (local, green):** new `WorkoutDetailSheet.test.tsx` (3: structured-bike breakdown + power profile, metadata-only non-bike, completed status) + 2 new `WeekAheadPage.test.tsx` cases (glance tap opens the sheet; editor tap opens the sheet, not the move picker); the refactored `StructuredWorkoutSheet.test.tsx` (6) + full `WeekAheadPage.test.tsx` (15) stayed green; web `tsc --noEmit` + shared `tsc --noEmit` clean; eslint 0 errors (6 known pre-existing Fast-Refresh warnings, none in the new files); production build clean (93 modules transformed, `✓ built`, Node 20). *The heaviest first-in-file `WeekAheadPage` integration test ("renders a move picker") hit the 5000ms default `userEvent` timeout on a cold esbuild transform but ran ~2s warm — a local-only cold-start sensitivity (cf. #122), not a regression; CI's own `Unit tests (web + shared)` job ran the full web vitest suite green in both waves.* **CI:** both branch-push and PR-context waves passed all 8 jobs — including the `Unit tests (web + shared)` job that runs the web vitest suite in CI — plus the Vercel preview. **Production on merge SHA `236dacbbbe2ddb886d90e44b616e61cbb3cb7386`:** Railway direct + Vercel same-origin `/api/v1/health` both served that SHA; **2026-07-16 — Closed out Batch 134 — Climate/bedroom subsystem resumes on the last holiday day — SHIPPED (PR #161, squash `709e72e`); production verified.** 🔴 High, Decision **#213**. The app now carries two holiday truths instead of one overloaded flag: inclusive `holiday.isActive` still tells the day/morning/last-night story, while end-exclusive `holiday.awayTonight` tells the evening bedroom/climate story. `holiday_pause.py` adds `holiday_windows_away_overnight(...)`, `overnight_away_window_for_date(...)`, and `HolidayPauseService.get_overnight_away_window_for_date(...)` using `start_date <= d < end_date`, leaving the existing inclusive helpers untouched. `DailyLoopService` computes both windows, `HolidayStateOut` plus `packages/shared/src/schemas.ts` document the new `holiday.awayTonight` field, and the overnight gates (`run_fan_control`, `run_evening_monitoring_alerts`, `run_evening_sleep_nudge`) now resume on `end_date` while staying dormant on `end_date-1`. The frontend switches only the *tonight* surfaces to `awayTonight` — Climate, Home's Tonight + Bedroom sections, Sleep Tonight, and the `protect-sleep` suppression — while Sleep Last night/history, the morning thermal gate, and the rest-day/holiday day semantics intentionally remain on inclusive `isActive`; **no migration**. **Verification:** local implementation stayed green (backend focused pytest **80 passed / 29 skipped**, backend `ruff check` clean, scoped backend `mypy` clean, shared vitest **19 passed** + shared `tsc --noEmit` clean, web focused vitest **102 passed**, web `tsc --noEmit` clean, production build clean). PR #161 needed one CI-only follow-up commit (`c1b1870`, `test: fix away-tonight holiday expectation`) after the first run exposed a stale `awayTonight` test expectation on `2026-07-14`; after that, both branch-push and PR-context CI waves passed all checks plus the Vercel preview. **Production on merge SHA `709e72efbe89a331011d8aae0c52a9e31678a1c0`:** Railway + Vercel same-origin `/api/v1/health` both served that SHA, web `/`, `/environment`, and `/sleep` returned `200`, and unauthenticated `GET /api/v1/daily-loop` returned `401` both direct and via Vercel. **Next:** no unshipped batch rows remain in `docs/phase-batches.md`; choose the next priority with Craig. **Deferred live-use:** the signed-in holiday-return evening eyeball still remains real-use verification.

**2026-07-16 — Closed out Batch 116 voice pick — SHIPPED (PR #158, squash `6fde062`); production verified.** 🟢 Mid, Decision **#210**. Swapped to `en_GB-northern_english_male-medium`, chosen by Craig from a live listening comparison, not a guess. Craig asked about celebrity voices (declined — unauthorized voice cloning of a real person is a real legal/ethical line, not just a scale question); offered ElevenLabs (~$22/mo for the app's real usage, researched live) as the actual path to meaningfully better quality, or trying more free Piper voices first. He chose Piper voices — pulled the real `voices.json` catalog (no more guessing paths), synthesized 6 candidates on the live container, and published them as an HTML artifact with embedded audio so Craig could actually listen and pick, rather than picking blind. His first choice (Ryan, `high` quality) benchmarked at 95s isolated for a full brief — combined with #197's finding that real production requests run ~2.4x slower than an isolated benchmark under CPU contention, that's a likely 150–230s+ in practice, so it was ruled out. Landed on Northern English Male (`medium`, 27.22s benchmarked — fastest of the three medium candidates tried, faster than the prior `alan-medium`'s 33.83s). **Confirmed in the real Railway build** (watched live via `railway logs --build`): the new voice's `curl` download succeeded, image built and passed its healthcheck. **Production on merge SHA `6fde06206da62b7d3c51ef632e18984538f9913a`:** Railway `/api/v1/health` served that SHA; web `/` returned `200`; unauthenticated `/api/v1/daily-loop` returned `401`. **Verification:** `ruff check`/`mypy` scoped to the touched `config.py` clean; no test changes needed (tests use fake `tmp_path` models, not the real filename). **Next:** ask Craig to try Listen once more and confirm the voice sounds better.

**2026-07-16 — Closed out Batch 131 — Strength watching-brief — SHIPPED (PR #157, squash `3cbd020`); production verified.** 🟢 Mid, Decision **#209**. Batch 131 was marked design-pending ("decide with Mark first" on what signal should drive the read and where it surfaces), but Craig chose to build a best-guess version and let Mark's feedback refine it rather than block on a design conversation. **Root cause was not missing data:** Batch 19 already computes a rolling 4w/12w strength frequency/duration/load-proxy rollup with a deterministic trend (`StrengthBriefService`, `apps/api/src/services/strength_brief.py`) and it was already on the daily-loop payload (`StrengthBriefOut`) — but the shared Zod `dailyLoopSchema` never declared a `strengthBrief` field, so the frontend silently dropped it and nothing ever surfaced it, unlike sibling `walkingBrief`/`breathworkBrief`. Reused the exact precedent already shipped for the same need — `WalkingBaseCard` on `/trends` — rather than inventing a new pattern: added `strengthBrief` to `dailyLoopSchema` (`packages/shared/src/schemas.ts`), a new `StrengthTrendCard` component (`apps/web/src/components/StrengthTrendCard.tsx`, copying `WalkingBaseCard`'s trend-badge + rolling-window-summary layout), wired onto `TrendsPage.tsx` below Walking base. No backend/service change — the engine already existed. **CI:** both branch-push and PR-context waves passed all 16 checks (8 jobs × 2 waves) plus the Vercel preview. **Production on merge SHA `3cbd0201675a997f1bd0f1bf1240004d72d2d64f`:** Railway direct + Vercel same-origin `/api/v1/health` both served that SHA; web `/` and `/trends` returned `200`; unauthenticated `/api/v1/daily-loop` returned `401` both direct and via Vercel. **Verification (local, green):** shared vitest **19 passed** + `tsc --noEmit` clean; web vitest **294 passed** (new: `TrendsPage.test.tsx` strength-trend assertions), `tsc --noEmit` clean, eslint clean (0 errors, 6 known warnings), production build clean (Node 20). No live-login browser check was done pre-merge — the local dev preview proxies to prod and this pass didn't have Mark's credentials; `TrendsPage.test.tsx`'s full-tree render with realistic mock data stood in. **Boundaries:** frontend + shared-schema only; no migration; no verdict/delivery/scheduler change; Green/Amber/Red, #133, #135, Red-never-VO2, strength recovery-isolation (#49/#80) untouched. **Open for Mark:** window length (4w/12w vs longer, since resistance work adapts slower) and whether load/duration should weight the trend, not just frequency — the built version is a best guess, not his confirmed scope. **No remaining unshipped batch in `docs/phase-batches.md`** — Batch 131 was the last ledger row.

**2026-07-15 — Batch 116 voice-quality follow-up SHIPPED (DECISIONS #197): hosted voice reverted from `low` back to `medium` quality.** 🟢 Mid. Craig heard the hosted voice for the first time after #195's CSP fix and reported it sounded "very robotic" (`low` quality, 16kHz). A live `railway ssh` benchmark against the real production container with realistic full-brief-length text (~2000 chars) showed `low` (23.27s) wasn't dramatically faster than `medium` (33.83s) — the earlier production 502 that justified downgrading to `low` (#193) was real, but the short test-phrase timing that made `low` look like a big speedup didn't hold at actual brief length. Reverted to `en_GB-alan-medium` (the original Batch 116 voice); `PIPER_TIMEOUT_SECONDS` raised 60→90s for headroom. **Merge note:** this shipped bundled inside PR #144 (Batch 120's squash-merge, `9cb43d6`) rather than its own PR — a `git checkout` race between two concurrent sessions sharing this working directory put this commit onto the Batch 120 branch's history before either PR merged; verified live in production regardless (health SHA `dd1d048` matches `origin/main`, `config.py` confirms `en_GB-alan-medium`). A duplicate PR (#145) was closed without merging once this was discovered. **Verification:** `ruff check`/`mypy` scoped to the touched files clean, targeted `test_piper_tts.py`/`test_tts.py` (4 passed, 6 DB-backed skipped locally). **Next:** ask Craig to try Listen again and confirm the voice sounds better and completes within the timeout.

**2026-07-14 — Closed out Batch 119 — Follow-up chat on a brief — SHIPPED (PR #142, squash `beb135c`); production verified.** 🟢 Mid, Decision **#194**. Kickoff decisions (119.3) made with Craig: **storage** is a new `brief_messages` table (018) keyed to `analysis_id` — same referential pattern as `Feedback` — not transient/in-memory history; **turn cap** is 10 user questions per brief (`MAX_USER_TURNS_PER_ANALYSIS`), a 422 past that; **action scope** is "chat can call existing propose endpoints only" via a **deterministic keyword check on Mark's own question** (never the model's answer) — a follow-up like "can you ease today's ride?" attaches `proposed_planned_workout_id` to the assistant turn only when there's a deliverable bike workout today and it isn't a rest day, and the frontend's "Propose this adjustment" button calls the *existing* `POST /api/v1/workout-delivery/planned-workouts/{id}/proposals` endpoint directly — Decision #29's propose→approve→push gate is untouched, this only adds a new entry point into its first step. **Backend:** `services/brief_chat.py` (`BriefChatService`, `SYSTEM_PROMPT` grounded in the brief's own stored `context_packet` + `output_markdown`, same floors as the morning prompt — Red-never-VO2, no L/R balance, local clock times, never narrate a skipped/holiday workout as live); `generate_anthropic_text` gained an optional `prior_messages` param (backward-compatible) so the same Anthropic boundary threads multi-turn history; `routers/brief_chat.py` — `GET`/`POST /api/v1/briefs/{analysis_id}/messages`, user-scoped (404/403) same as feedback. Migration 018 (`brief_messages` table) + 019 (RLS ENABLE, since it's the first new coach table since migration 015 — `test_coach_rls_migration.py` was generalized to check a list of RLS migrations, not just 015, so future new tables follow the same pattern). **Frontend:** `BriefFollowUpChat.tsx` renders on `MorningBriefPage` below the coach read — question box, threaded history, and the conditional propose button; shared `briefMessage*` Zod schemas/types in `@coach/shared`. **CI caught two real bugs the first push missed** (both test-only, no production-code fix needed): the deterministic keyword-match test used `workoutType: "bike"`, which `is_bike_workout_type` doesn't recognize (it matches the `bike_*` enum, e.g. `bike_sweet_spot`); and the same test inserted a `brief_messages` row with a fabricated `proposed_planned_workout_id` UUID, tripping the real FK to `planned_workouts` under actual Postgres (SQLite/mocked paths wouldn't have caught this) — fixed by persisting a real `PlannedWorkout` row. **CI:** both branch-push and PR-context waves passed all 8 checks (7 jobs + Vercel) each on the corrected commit. **Production on merge SHA `beb135c7008991b3d18079fe34bdd55b5cedb028`:** Railway + Vercel same-origin `/api/v1/health` both served that SHA; web `/` and `/brief` returned `200`; unauthenticated `/api/v1/daily-loop` returned `401` both direct and via Vercel. **Boundaries:** no change to Green/Amber/Red, #133, #135, the morning brief's own prompt/generation path, or the propose→approve→push contract itself. **Next:** no unshipped rows remain in `docs/phase-batches.md` as of this closeout; pick the next priority with Craig. **Deferred live-use:** the phone eyeball of actually asking a follow-up question and, on a day with a deliverable ride, tapping "Propose this adjustment" remains deferred — CI can't exercise a live Anthropic call or a real device thread, consistent with prior batches' deferred-eyeball posture.

**2026-07-14 — Closed out the Batch 116 Piper voice/timeout hotfix — SHIPPED (PR #141, squash `fe337dc`); production verified, including the real Railway build.** 🟢 Mid, Decision **#193**. Craig tried the hosted voice toggle and heard nothing; `railway logs --http` showed `POST /api/v1/tts/synthesize 502 46427ms` — Piper's `medium`-tier synthesis exceeded the 45s internal timeout for a full brief on Railway's shared CPU. **2026-07-14 — Closed out the Batch 116 engine amendment — self-hosted Piper replaces OpenAI TTS — SHIPPED (PR #138, squash `ba7b509`); production verified, including a real Railway container build.** 🟢 Mid, Decision **#190**. Craig asked what `OPENAI_API_KEY` would cost right after Batch 116 shipped, learned it wasn't free, and asked for a free alternative — self-hosted Piper was the option offered but not chosen at the original kickoff (higher build cost then; that tradeoff reads differently now cost is the deciding factor). **Not a reversal of #189:** the consent-gated, off-by-default, automatic-on-device-fallback design is unchanged — only the engine behind `POST /api/v1/tts/synthesize` changes. `services/piper_tts.py` replaces `services/openai_tts.py`, shelling out to the `piper` CLI (pip package `piper-tts`) rather than its Python API for stability across releases; a British voice model (`en_GB-alan-medium`) is baked into the Dockerfile at build time from the public `rhasspy/piper-voices` repo; `config.py`'s `openai_*` settings become `piper_voice_model_path`/`piper_voice_config_path`; response `Content-Type` moves from `audio/mpeg` to `audio/wav`. **This project's CI installs Python deps directly with pip, it doesn't build the Dockerfile** — so green CI only confirmed `piper-tts` installs and the code/tests are correct, not that the real container build works; merge was deliberately paused for an explicit go-ahead, then the actual Railway build was watched live via `railway logs --build` rather than trusted blind. **Confirmed in the real build:** `piper-tts==1.4.2` + `onnxruntime` installed cleanly; both `curl -fsSL` steps for `en_GB-alan-medium.onnx`/`.onnx.json` succeeded (a bad URL would have failed the `RUN` and the whole build); the image built, pushed, and passed its healthcheck. **Production on merge SHA `ba7b50997fbe23d50c5692bf9c69d80d57e5130f`:** Railway `/api/v1/health` served that SHA; web `/` returned `200`; unauthenticated `/api/v1/daily-loop` returned `401` both direct and via Vercel. **Still unverified:** the actual synthesized audio quality/correctness — the build succeeding proves the model file downloaded and `piper` is installed, not that a real `POST /api/v1/tts/synthesize` call (with `Profile.hosted_tts_consent = true`) produces a good WAV; that needs a live check with a real user turning the Settings toggle on. **Next:** Batch **117** (Sleep calendar day-stepping) is the next unshipped row in `docs/phase-batches.md`; separately, a live synthesize call against production would close the loop on Piper's actual audio quality.

`daily-loop` payload gains `hostedTtsConsent: bool`. **Frontend:** `BriefListenControls.tsx` tries the hosted path first when consent is on, falls back to on-device `SpeechSynthesis` on any failure; new Settings "Voice" section with the off-by-default toggle. **Boundaries:** the on-device default path (#179/#184) is unchanged; **2026-07-14 — Closed out Batch 111 — Natural read-aloud voice — SHIPPED (PR #132, squash `c90f825`).** 🟢 Mid, Decision **#184**. Settled the kickoff fork (111.2) as on-device over hosted TTS: Decision #179 chose the browser's `SpeechSynthesis` API specifically to keep the brief's health-data text off third-party servers, and better voice quality alone doesn't outweigh that, so this batch stays inside the same API and fixes the actual complaint — the default voice sounding robotic — by picking a better voice rather than a better backend. New pure `selectBestVoice(voices, targetLang)` (`apps/web/src/lib/speechVoice.ts`) scores `getVoices()` results by locale match then a quality-keyword name bonus (`natural`/`neural`/`premium`/`enhanced`), but only ever considers `localService === true` voices — Chrome's default "Google UK English" style voices report through the same API surface but actually synthesize on Google's servers, so including them would have quietly reintroduced the exact leak #179 avoided; when nothing local matches the target language it returns `null` and `BriefListenControls` leaves the platform's own default voice in place, unchanged from pre-batch behavior. **CI:** both branch-push and PR-context waves passed all 7 jobs plus the Vercel preview. **Production on merge SHA `c90f825aad1190e080072b887b973ca63d607120`:** Railway + Vercel same-origin `/api/v1/health` both served that SHA; web `/` and `/brief` returned `200`; unauthenticated `/api/v1/daily-loop` returned `401` both direct and via Vercel. **Boundaries:** frontend-only, no API/shared-schema/migration change; no hosted TTS integration; #179's privacy posture unchanged; Green/Amber/Red, #133, #135, Red-never-VO2 untouched. **Next:** Batch **112** (notification cleanup: stale `/bedroom` routes + redundant brief push) is the next unshipped row in `docs/phase-batches.md`. **Deferred live-use:** the real-device voice-quality eyeball remains deferred — voice availability/quality is OS/browser-dependent and can't be verified headlessly, same as Batch 106's original playback eyeball.

**2026-07-11 — Closed out Batch 80 — "Was overriding the plan the right call?" deviation verdict — SHIPPED (PR #105, squash `1598d12`); production verified.** 🔴 High, Decision **#153**, batch row `docs/phase-batches.md` (Batch 80). **The problem it solves (Mark's Q1a):** when Mark does his own thing instead of the plan, the post-ride read graded the ride but never said plainly whether the override was a good call or a setback. **What it does (backend-only, `services/post_workout_analysis.py`):** a new pure `detect_ride_deviation(...)` runs inside `assemble_context_packet` and attaches a deterministic `rideDeviation` block to the packet, reusing the Batch 68 delivered-vs-actual grade (`execution`) as the objective anchor. It flags a divergence **only** when a bike session was actually planned/delivered and he didn't do it as prescribed: `skipped_and_rode` (day's bike workout `status='skipped'` but a ride completed), or `easier_than_planned` / `harder_than_planned` (every gradable work interval off target in the *same* direction — a real attempt lands ≥1 interval on target, so a fade is *not* flagged). It never flags an **approved coach-adjustment** (Batch 68 `adjustment.changed` / Batch 69 `actualWorkoutJson.source='accepted_adjustment'` → `wasApprovedAdjustment`) and never flags a **no-plan free ride** (`free_ride`, so spontaneous rides stay unflagged). The packet carries the `kind`/`reason`, objective `signals` (work/on/over/under counts), the planned-vs-actual summary, and `morningReadiness` (the day's morning verdict), so the good-call/bad-call *judgement* is the prompt's, anchored on readiness + numbers. `SYSTEM_PROMPT` gains the deviation-verdict instruction — explicitly forbidding softening a poor call into praise or inventing a problem where the call was sound (the one place it must not be sycophantic) — plus three output rules; `PROMPT_VERSION` → `post-workout-analysis-v5-2026-07-11` (regenerates older reads via the existing `_analysis_is_current` staleness check). The verdict flows through the existing post-workout `output_markdown`, so **no frontend/shared change, no migration**. **Boundaries:** no delivery write, no grade-math change; Green/Amber/Red, #133, #135, and Red-never-VO2 all untouched (no morning/verdict/executable-coaching code changed). **Scope call:** an unplanned ride on a no-bike-plan day is a free ride, not an override — flagging every casual ride would be noise, and Q1a presupposes a plan to override. **Gates (local, all green):** backend pytest **565 passed / 192 skipped** (7 new pure `detect_ride_deviation` cases run locally — easier/harder/on-plan-attempt/skipped/approved-adjustment/free-ride/ungradable-no-false-positive; 3 new DB-backed `assemble_context_packet` integration cases — self-chosen easy ride on a Red day, skipped key session on a Green day, on-plan sweet-spot → no deviation — plus approved-adjustment + free-ride assertions folded into the existing Batch 68/free-ride tests, all run in CI), backend ruff check + `ruff format --check` clean, `mypy src` clean (103 files). No local Postgres/docker here, so the DB-backed cases skipped locally and proved out in CI (established pattern). **Closeout:** PR #105 CI went green across all 7 jobs in both push and PR-context waves plus a successful Vercel preview; squash-merged to `main` as `1598d12f2bfee33c0a090b9363a7c3fe57e6d0c4`. **Production verified on the merge SHA:** Railway and Vercel same-origin `/api/v1/health` (`garmin-coach-one.vercel.app`) both returned `1598d12…`, web `/` and `/delivery` returned 200, and unauthenticated `GET /api/v1/daily-loop` returned 401 both direct and via Vercel (the deviation verdict rides in that auth-gated payload's downstream post-workout read; no new endpoint). **Deferred to live use:** the deviation copy itself is a phone eyeball on the next genuinely diverged ride — automated smoke can't exercise a Claude-written `output_markdown`. **Next step:** Batch **81** (Calendar-aware week view, 🟢 Mid — surface each week's block character/holiday + Holiday/Builder entry points on the organiser; no migration) is the next unshipped row in `docs/phase-batches.md`; then Batch **82** (Reset-week control, 🔴 High) and Batch **83** (one-tap week restructure, 🟢 Mid, depends on 81). Or pick the next priority with Craig. **Open (carried):** (a) `garmin-coach.vercel.app` stale alias — use `garmin-coach-one.vercel.app`; (b) RLS disabled on `coach.*` tables; (c) genuine POOR-readiness days remain a coaching/data question; (d) runtime coaching model still `claude-sonnet-4-6`; (e) the Batch 78 Garmin device spot-check remains deferred to live use.

**Prior — Batch 71 - Editable quick-add on the Week tab - SHIPPED (PR #96, squash `b37e01d`), prod-verified.** 🟢 Mid, Decision **#144**, spec `docs/designs/workout-fidelity-and-feedback-loop.md` (Newly surfaced section) — Mark's 2026-07-09 sign-off feedback: tapping "+ Cycle / + Weights / + Flexibility" on `/delivery` always dropped a hardcoded 45-min Zone-2 ride with no picker and no edit. **What it does:** a small per-category subtype catalog (`QUICK_ADD_CATALOG` in `services/plan_actions.py`) — cycle: endurance/sweet_spot/recovery; weights: maintenance/recovery; flexibility: mobility only — each with a title, workout type, intensity target, default duration, and a `[min,max]` duration bound. `workout_for_selection` resolves the chosen option, validates the duration against its bound (422 outside range), and builds the `structured_workout` (bike: warm-up/main/cool-down sized to sum to the chosen duration). `add_workout` / `POST /days/{date}/workouts` accept optional `subtype` + `durationMin`; omitting both preserves the exact prior hardcoded-default behaviour (first catalog entry), so no existing caller regresses. **Prior — Batch 70 - Weekly-mix maintenance & dynamic rebalancing - SHIPPED (PR #95, squash `7598b6f`), prod-verified.** 🔴 High, Decision **#143**, spec `docs/designs/workout-fidelity-and-feedback-loop.md` — the last spec'd batch in the workout-fidelity thread and the one genuinely new feature (Mark's observation 4: "if it drops the VO2 for an easier Z2, does it notice no VO2 was done this week and patch it back in?"). **What it does:** the morning verdict now tracks his weekly quality mix (**VO2×1 / Sweet-Spot×1 / Zone-2×3**, derived from his own plan) as a **soft, readiness-gated quota** — the mix is a protected target, readiness gets the veto, and any shortfall is made visible and explained rather than forced or hidden (confirmed by Mark 2026-07-09). New pure `services/weekly_mix.py`: `summarize_weekly_mix` is a deterministic reducer over the week's planned + completed bike rows reporting per bucket the plan-derived `target` (a recovery week with no VO2 reads `target=0` — never a phantom shortfall), `done` (`PlannedWorkout.status=='completed'`), `due`, and `at_risk` when what's owed exceeds what's genuinely still scheduled (today's eased hard session stops counting as a scheduled slot). When an Amber/Red morning eases today's hard bike session, the verdict either **re-patches** it to a sound later day this week (reusing the Batch 66 `plan_swap_first` swap engine — the same one-tap category-scoped `swap_day`) or says plainly **"no VO2 this week — readiness gets the veto"**, appended to `planAdjustments`; Batch 66's pure callers are unchanged). `PROMPT_VERSION`→`morning-analysis-v7-2026-07-09` (regenerates stale reads). `AnalysisOut.weeklyMix` + shared `weeklyMixSchema` surface it; a reusable `WeeklyMixCard` renders done/target chips on the Home Today card and the `/delivery` Plan page (the Plan page also shows the shortfall message, reading `daily-loop.morningAnalysis.weeklyMix`). **Boundaries:** advisory only — nothing auto-schedules; **no migration** (derived read-only accounting over existing rows); Green/Amber/Red, #133, #135, Red-never-VO2, and the ≥2-day no-stack rule all untouched; empty-day *insertion* of a make-up session is out of scope (needs Batch 71's editable quick-add) — the re-patch only trades with an existing easier bike day. **Gates (local, all green):** backend pytest **537 passed / 173 skipped** (new `test_weekly_mix.py` — bucket mapping, plan-derived target, past-miss vs future-slot, eased-today at-risk, `_eased_bucket` gating, re-patch/not-this-week shortfall, 3 DB-backed service cases; **Prior — Batch 67 - Real structured workouts + harden delivery parsing - IMPLEMENTED on `feat/batch-67-structured-workouts` (verified locally, NOT yet shipped).** 🔴 High, Decision **#140**, spec `docs/designs/workout-fidelity-and-feedback-loop.md` — the trunk fix of Mark's 2026-07-07/08 workout-fidelity feedback (67 makes the workouts real; 68-70 build on it). **The problem:** every one of the 65 bike sessions in `apps/api/data/plans/plan_no2.json` was authored as a **single collapsed block** (`{label, target: <prose>, minutes: <total>}`), the real structure living only in an unparsed `summary` string — so the parser delivered the VO2 day as a **flat 55%/154 W Z1 ride** (the `return 55` fallback on `"VO₂ (see prescription)"`), Z2 at the **top of its band** (an en-dash defeated band-averaging → 72% not 68%), and durations that had drifted (VO2 `60` vs the real ~47). **What it does now:** **(67.1)** `_expand_step` (`workout_delivery.py`) gains a **ramp raw-step form** `{"label","minutes","ramp":[start,end]}` → a genuine ramp IR step (`powerStartPct != powerEndPct`); it previously could only emit *steady* steps, so every warm-up landed flat. **(67.2)** `_power_pct` no longer `return 55`s on an unresolvable target — it **raises 422** (the named-zone map, e.g. `"easy spin"→50`, is kept for existing callers); new pure `expand_structured_steps` + `validate_deliverable_bike_workout` are called from `build_plan_rows`, so a bike workout that can't resolve, is single-block, lacks a warm-up/cool-down/ramp, **or whose `duration_min` doesn't trace the summed steps fails at import — before Zwift.** **(67.3)** the band regex accepts the unicode dash family and collapses a band to its **midpoint** — `"65–72%"` → **68%**, so a 64.9% ride grades "on" (±5) not "under" vs 72. **(67.2b)** all **65** `bike_*` workouts were re-authored from the source doc `~/Downloads/Dad Fitness/Full 13 Wk. 2121 Plan No. 2 Start 06.07.26.docx` (the lossy JSON `summary` strings were **not** trusted) into multi-step `steps` (warm-up ramp → priming pattern → work interval(s) at explicit % → recovery valleys → cool-down), `duration_min` = the true summed steps; VO2 uses recovery-after-each-rep (spec's ~47-min figure), the Sat neuromuscular block is `6 × (12 s @185% + 2:48 @55%)`, endurance ranges are en-dash bands resolving to their midpoint (**Long Z2 68%, easy/recovery Z2 62%**). **Decided (Mark 2026-07-09):** day placement stays **Dumbbells Mon / Bodyweight Sat as separate movable rows** (Batch 65 preserved — a semantic diff confirmed all 35 non-bike/rest rows are byte-identical; only the 65 bike days changed); **FTP 280 W**; Mon/Fri "no hard bike" is Batch 70's concern. **Method:** transcription ran through a throwaway generator (scratchpad, not committed) that mutates only bike days in place and validates each via the real engine; the committed artifact is the reviewed JSON, independently locked by the new `test_plan_fidelity.py`. **Boundaries:** **no migration** (data + parser only); verdict / #133 / #135 / Red-never-VO2 untouched; no per-interval editor UI (the manual-override intensity dial stays the escape hatch); `build_structured_workout_ir` is behaviourally unchanged for callers — it now delegates to `expand_structured_steps`. **Gates (local, all green):** backend pytest **528 passed / 168 skipped** (new `test_plan_fidelity.py` shape guard: 65-bike count, total-time trace, no-flat-55, midpoint bands, VO2-as-120% intervals, import-gate accept/reject; +10 grammar/parser/ZWO-snapshot cases in `test_workout_delivery.py`), ruff check + `ruff format --check` clean, mypy **98 files** clean; shared typecheck + **13** tests; web `tsc` clean, lint 0 errors (6 pre-existing Fast-Refresh warnings), vitest **181 passed / 30 files**, build clean under Node 20 (web/shared untouched by this backend-only batch). Verified end-to-end locally: a VO2 workout delivers as `<Warmup>` ramp + 5×2 min @120% `SteadyState` intervals + `<Cooldown>` ramp (not a flat block), and an unresolvable target raises 422. **Next step:** commit + push the branch, open the PR; **67.4 is an explicit `/closeout` step (not run at batch-start):** re-import **forward from the resume Monday** (`python -m src.plan_import apps/api/data/plans/plan_no2.json --start-date <resume-Monday>`) so the reset/off week isn't clobbered, then `reconcile_deliveries` re-pushes the corrected bike rows + a Zwift spot-check that the VO2 shows intervals with ramps. Then Batches **68** (grade the delivered IR), **69** (accept=logged; move session-logging post-ride), **70** (weekly-mix rebalancing) remain `Planned`. **Open (carried):** (a) `garmin-coach.vercel.app` stale alias `/api/*` 404 — use `garmin-coach-one.vercel.app` for same-origin smoke; (b) RLS disabled on 16 `coach.*` tables; (c) genuine POOR-readiness days remain a coaching/data question; (d) runtime coaching model still `claude-sonnet-4-6`.

**Prior — Batch 62 — First-open latency: persist cache & thin daily-loop — SHIPPED (PR #86, squash `8a60a76`); production HTTP smoke pending manual confirmation.** 🔴 High, Decision **#136** (spec `docs/designs/first-open-performance.md`). Fixes "data is slow to load when I first open the app" — measured first: warm prod `/api/v1/health` is ~0.10 s, so it is **not** a container cold-start; the real causes are an empty client cache on a fresh PWA launch + `GET /api/v1/daily-loop` being the fattest endpoint. **What it does:** **(62.1)** `App.tsx` swaps to `PersistQueryClientProvider` (new `lib/queryClient.ts` centralises client + persister + `clearPersistedCache()`), persisting **only** a successful `daily-loop` query to `localStorage` with `maxAge` 24 h + `buster`=build SHA (vite `define __APP_BUSTER__` ← `VERCEL_GIT_COMMIT_SHA`); `useDailyLoop` gets `staleTime` 60 s; login/activate/unlock/logout clear the persisted cache alongside `queryClient.clear()`. All three `@tanstack` packages pinned to `5.101.2` to dedupe `query-core`. **(62.2)** `run_morning_weather_sync` precomputes the 120-day driver correlation once via new `InsightsService.record_drivers` (stored in the existing `analyses` `driver_correlation` audit row, **no migration**); `_envelope` reads it back via `cached_drivers`, falling back to live compute when absent — payload identical, only *when* it's computed moves. **(62.3)** the four post-`{workout,flexibility,strength,walk}` analysis SELECTs collapse into one `analysis_type IN (...)` query partitioned in Python, order-preserving. **(62.4)** new `run_connection_warmup` job runs `SELECT 1` every 10 min inside the 30-min `pool_recycle`. **(62.5)** the daily-loop GET handler logs `snapshot_ms`/`envelope_ms`/`total_ms`. **Scope deviation (documented in #136):** the spec's brief-parallelization half of 62.3 was **built then reverted** — separate `AsyncSessionLocal()` sessions break read-your-writes within the request transaction (the identical-payload snapshot test caught it) and the win is marginal for 1–2 users; only the safe SELECT collapse ships (the spec sanctions this staging). **Boundaries:** no verdict/analysis/sleep-scoring/#133/#134/#135/Red-never-VO2 change — *when*/*how fast*, never *what*. No migration. New health data at rest in `localStorage` (bounded by `maxAge` + daily-loop-only dehydrate + logout clear). **Verification (all local, green):** backend full pytest **658 passed** against a local UTF8 Postgres (incl. new identical-payload/read-through/collapse tests; earlier `SQL_ASCII` local runs mismatched CI encoding — recreating the DB as UTF8 matched CI and went green), ruff + `ruff format --check` clean, mypy **96 files** clean; shared typecheck + **12** tests; web `tsc` clean, lint **0 errors** (6 known Fast-Refresh warnings), full web vitest **172 passed** (new `lib/queryClient.test.ts`), web build clean under Node 22. **Closeout status:** PR #86 CI went **fully green** across all 7 jobs (backend pytest/ruff/mypy, Alembic migration check, security audit, web build, web+shared vitest) in **both** push and PR contexts, plus a successful Vercel preview deploy; squash-merged to `main` as `8a60a76`. **Production HTTP smoke NOT run from this environment** — the agent egress policy denies CONNECT (403) to `api-production-e2bc7.up.railway.app` and `garmin-coach.vercel.app`, so the standard merge-SHA smoke (Railway + Vercel same-origin `/api/v1/health` returns `8a60a76…`, web `/` 200, unauthenticated `GET /api/v1/daily-loop` 401 direct + via Vercel) and the before/after `railway run` daily-loop timing + Railway↔Supabase colocation check must be run by Craig from a permitted network. **Deploy risk is low:** no migration (schema unchanged at `012`), and the Vercel preview already built the frontend clean. **Next step:** Craig confirms the prod smoke + captures the daily-loop timing; then the daily-flow/summary-feedback/scheduling plans (Batches 63–66, all `Planned`) are the open frontier. **Open (carried, Craig's call):** (a) 🔒 RLS disabled on 16 `coach.*` tables; (b) genuine POOR-readiness days are a separate coaching/data question; (c) runtime coaching model still `claude-sonnet-4-6`.

A new `lib/truncate.ts` (`truncateWords`) truncates collapsed summaries on a word boundary instead of a mid-word CSS ellipsis. `CollapsibleSection`'s body now animates in with `framer-motion` (fade + settle, honouring `prefers-reduced-motion` via the same `useReducedMotionConfig` hook `score-input.tsx` already uses). **Verification:** local rerun green (`pnpm --dir apps/web test` → **137 passed / 28 files**; `pnpm --dir apps/web lint` → 0 errors / 6 known Fast-Refresh warnings; `pnpm --dir apps/web build` clean under Node 20). **Batch 52 — Design foundations (token + primitive tier) — SHIPPED (PR #72, squash `41f6734`), prod-verified.** Frontend-only, no backend/payload change, no migration (DECISIONS #122; spec `docs/designs/design-foundations.md`). The **first** of the four front-end premium batches (52–55) and the load-bearing one 53–55 inherit — it lifts the shipped design system from "developer-dark" to "calm premium" at the **token + primitive layer only**, with no per-screen layout change. **What it does:** (1) **re-spaces the dark surface/border ramp** into a clear value ramp — `bg #0A1112→#0A1314`, `surface #111E1F→#152628`, `elevated #192A2B→#1F383A`, `overlay #213436→#294648`, `border #253A3C→#2E4C4E`, `border-strong #345355→#3D5F61` (each surface step ~+8 CIELab L\* vs the old ~+5, chosen by a throwaway CIELab/WCAG evaluator not eyeballing), keeping the teal-graphite hue; **shadows softened** (value carries depth, not glossy drop-shadows) and the focus `--shadow-glow` strengthened 0.25→0.35; (2) **redesigns the input/control tier** — new `--control`/`--control-border` fill (`#223C3E`/`#436769` dark, `#FFFFFF`/`#CBD2D9` light) so inputs are raised, legible fields (was dark-on-dark `bg-bg`), applied to `Input`, a **new shared `Textarea` primitive** (replacing the two ad-hoc `textareaClassName` copies in `DashboardPage`/`CheckInPage`), and `Select` (trigger on control fill; dropdown → elevated, item-hover → overlay); **text AA held in both palettes** — dark muted `#7B859B→#98A2B4` + secondary `#94A3B8→#A6B4C4` (clears AA ≥4.6:1 even on the control fill, ordering preserved), and **light muted `#8A93A1→#6B7280` fixes a real pre-existing AA failure** (~2.8:1 on white); (3) **pulls mono-uppercase back to eyebrows** — the `Label` primitive is now sentence-case at `text-sm`, with a documented type scale added to `index.css`. `theme/tokens.ts` mirrors every value (and its stale teal `shadow.glow` was synced to the emerald CSS var); `tailwind.config.ts` exposes the `control` utilities; the PWA/status-bar `theme-color` (index.html meta + pre-mount script, `ThemeContext`, manifest) synced to `#0A1314`. **`Card`/`Button` were left unedited on purpose** — they consume the changed tokens (`bg-surface`/`border-*`/`shadow-sm`) so the wider ramp + stronger borders flow in without class churn. **Verification (local, all green under Node 20):** new `components/ui/controls.test.tsx` (4 cases: control-fill on Input/Textarea, prop/min-h forwarding, sentence-case Label); `tsc --noEmit` clean; web lint **0 errors** (6 Fast-Refresh warnings — the 5 pre-existing + one for `input.tsx`'s new exported const, same benign class as `buttonVariants`); full web vitest **118 passed / 23 files** (114 prior + 4 new); web build clean under Node 20; backend/shared untouched. **Live-verified** in a headless preview against a temporary prod-free mock `/api` (reverted before commit): Home, Check-in, Sleep at 375×812 in **dark + light** — dark surfaces now visibly separate (hero, section cards, nested wells, table header), Check-in inputs are legible raised fields with readable placeholders, labels render sentence-case, and the light palette's separation is intact. **Drive-by fix (test-only, documented in #122):** `DashboardPage.test.tsx` was flaky-by-clock — `isEveningNow()` reads `getHours() >= 20` and the daytime tests never mocked the clock, so **11 of them fail on `main` whenever the local `pnpm test` runs after 20:00 local**. **CI does not run web vitest** (web CI = lint + typecheck + vite build only), so this never blocked CI — Batch 51 shipped green because its *local* run happened earlier in the day, not from CI coverage. Fixed with a `beforeEach` freezing the wall-clock to a daytime instant (the one evening test keeps its 21:30 override) so the local gate is deterministic. (That CI gap is **now closed** — PR #73 / `e41c81c` added a `test-web` CI job running `pnpm -r test` across web + shared, so web/shared vitest regressions now fail CI.) **PR #72 CI went green** across backend pytest/ruff/mypy, Alembic migration check, security audit, the web build (lint + typecheck + vite), and the Vercel preview; squash-merged to `main` as `41f6734`. **Production verified on merge SHA `41f6734`:** Railway and Vercel same-origin `/api/v1/health` both returned `sha=41f6734758bac1d6b8bc6ed0f8a2cde46ea005ef`, web `/` and the restyled `/check-in` route both returned 200, and `GET /api/v1/daily-loop` returned 401 unauthenticated both direct and via the Vercel rewrite (non-mutating auth-gated smoke; this batch adds no new endpoint — it is frontend-render only, so the live proof is the served web deploy on the merge SHA). **Current follow-up:** Batch 53 is now shipped; the remaining front-end premium batches are **Batch 54 — Home hierarchy & calm density** and **Batch 55 — Screen polish & states**, in that order.

The third and last of the Home & navigation UX batches (49–51) — Craig confirmed at `/batch-start` to build it despite Mark being phone-only, so **the Home & navigation UX plan (49–51) is now fully shipped.** **What it does:** on `md+` viewports, Home's six sections split into an **act lane** (Today, After your ride, Tomorrow) and a **context lane** (Last night, Tonight, Bedroom); mobile is unchanged. CSS Grid's own auto-placement then stacks each lane in `orderedSections`' existing order with no extra logic, and the current primary (Batch 50 action or Batch 48 phase) stays first in its lane because it's already first in the flat `order` array. **One DOM tree, no duplicate render** — mobile's `grid-cols-1` collapses to the exact pre-batch single stacked column, so section open/collapsed state can never diverge across a resize. **Same-PR follow-on (a copy fix, not a design decision — no new decision number):** the Next-strip/Today-footer "Check in" label was ambiguous against the per-ride "How did it feel?" check-in already on the After-your-ride card, so `lib/homeActions.ts`'s rung 3 now labels `'Morning check-in'` (was the bare `'Check in'`) and rung 2 names the specific ride — `` `Log how ${activityName} felt` `` (falls back to `'your ride'` when the analysed activity has no name) instead of the generic `'Log how your ride felt'`; the same-route static fallback link in `DashboardPage.tsx`'s Today footer picked up the `'Morning check-in'` wording too. **Verification (local, all green):** new `sectionLane` tests in `homeSections.test.ts`; **Prior — Batch 50 — Action-first Home — SHIPPED (PR #70, squash `8542e4a`), prod-verified.** Frontend-only, no backend/payload change, no migration (DECISIONS #120; spec `docs/designs/action-first-home.md`). The second of the Home & navigation UX batches (49–51) — catches the **Home page** up to being push-first (Batch 45). **What it does:** a new pure, payload-only `lib/homeActions.ts` (`nextAction(data, {isEvening})` → `{key,label,to?,sectionKey?,tone}` + `actionSection`) resolves the single "what needs Mark next" action from a deterministic ladder — **pending coach change** (`delivery.changed && isBike`, → expand `today`) > **unlogged ride check-in** (`postWorkoutAnalyses` item with `postRideCheckIn==null`, → expand `afterRide`) > **no daily check-in** (`!manualEntry`, → `/check-in`) > **evening & `sleepProjection.tone==='protect'`** (→ `/sleep`) > **all-clear** ("You're all set"). It drives (a) a new **"Next" strip** under `VerdictHero` (a labelled region; the all-clear state is a quiet button-less status line) that replaces the lone Check-in button, and (b) an **override of the Batch 37/48 phase→primary selection** — `orderedSections` gained an optional `primary` param so `actionSection(nextAction) ?? primarySection(phase,{hasRide})` both **leads** the order and is the one `defaultOpen`, so the pending-action section is expanded regardless of time of day (rungs 1–3 are clock-independent; only protect-sleep is evening-gated). `CollapsibleSection` gained a `tone` prop (a `bg-warning` "needs a tap" dot while collapsed) + an `id` (so the strip scrolls to a section-target action); `todaySummary`/`afterRideSummary` now return `{text,tone}` (Today→warning on a pending change, After-your-ride→warning on an unlogged check-in); the **duplicated Today verdict badge is dropped** (VerdictHero canonical); Home's evening `tonight`/`bedroom` become compact cards deep-linking into the Batch 49 Sleep hub (Bedroom's link shipped in 49; Tonight gains a `DetailLinkCard` at the Home section level so the shared `SleepPrepBody` doesn't self-link on `/sleep`); and Check-in stays reachable via a fallback link in the Today footer. **Decisions settled at `/batch-start` (per spec):** action-over-phase *always* (not morning-only); the ladder order above; one primary action (Check-in demoted); revises-not-replaces Batch 37/48 (phase stays the fallback). **Boundaries kept:** every signal already rides `/api/v1/daily-loop` — no new endpoint/payload/migration; exactly one section expanded (need first, time second); no push logic (that's Batch 45 — this only *surfaces* the action). **The `ignored` note:** the resolver keys the pending-change rung on the payload's `delivery.changed && isBike` only — the client-only Ignore dismiss (#99) isn't persisted and the change is still pending until approved, so the strip honestly reflects the payload. **Verification (local, all green):** `tsc --noEmit` clean; web lint 0 errors (the same 5 pre-existing Fast-Refresh warnings); full web vitest **109 passed / 22 files** (new `homeActions.test.ts` = 11 pure cases; `homeSections.test.ts` +3 override cases; `DashboardPage.test.tsx` verdict-once fix + 3 new: check-in strip default, action-override-expands-Today + collapsed warning dot, all-clear strip); web build clean under **Node 20** (local Node 18 trips the pre-existing `vite-plugin-pwa`/`workbox` issue); backend + shared suites untouched (only `apps/web/src/**` changed). **Shipped:** PR #70 CI went green across backend pytest/ruff/mypy, Alembic migration check, security audit, web build, and the Vercel preview; squash-merged to `main` as `8542e4a`. **Production verified on merge SHA `8542e4a`:** Railway and Vercel same-origin `/api/v1/health` both returned `sha=8542e4a0d382f3052ed5c440187c4465b686fbea`, web `/` and the Batch 49 `/sleep` route both returned 200, and `GET /api/v1/daily-loop` returned 401 unauthenticated both direct and via the Vercel rewrite (non-mutating auth-gated smoke; this batch adds no new endpoint — the change is Home-render only). **Visual review** was covered by the deterministic vitest mount tests (they assert the Next strip per state, the action-over-phase expansion, the collapsed warning dot, and the dropped verdict badge) plus the green Vercel preview build, rather than a separate mock-`/api` headless session; **Prior — Batch 48 — Explicit daily/block loop model — SHIPPED (PR #68, squash `d9060a1`), prod-verified.** The optional consolidating refactor that closes the passive-first plan (DECISIONS #118; spec `docs/designs/explicit-loop-model.md`). **Scope settled with Craig at `/batch-start`:** Batch 48 is explicitly optional/deferrable and Batches 45–47 had shipped cleanly + prod-verified, so of the ledger's options Craig chose **"model + frontend, no rewire"** — build the loop-state model + orchestration seam and ship the user-visible generalisation, but **leave the prod-verified 45–47 push/projection/block wiring untouched** (it can adopt the seam later). **What it adds:** a pure DB-free `services/daily_loop_state.py` — `DayPhase = rest_day | pre_training | post_training | wind_down` (precedence: evening `wind_down` → `post_training` off *any* ride/strength/flexibility/walk read → `rest_day` → `pre_training`), `BlockPhase` classified from the active block (`consolidation` = the explicit end-of-block boundary, the Batch 47 trigger), and `describe_loop_state(...)` as the "where is Mark + what's next" seam. It generalises the cycling-shaped `post_ride` (a strength/walk-only day now advances instead of being stuck `pre_ride`) and makes evening a first-class `wind_down` phase instead of the 20:00 clock-reorder hack. The daily-loop payload gains a read-only `loopState { dayPhase, blockPhase, nextAction, atBlockBoundary }` (derived in `DailyLoopService` from post-session counts + planned workouts + the profile-local clock + a cheap new `_active_block` query); the generalised `useDailyPhase` **prefers** the server data stage with a local fallback and applies the live-clock `wind_down` overlay itself; `homeSections` swaps its phase→section map for a `hasRide`-aware `primarySection` (non-ride `post_training` leads with the Today card where those reads render; `wind_down` leads with Tonight); `DashboardPage` threads **one** `isEveningNow()` read through both phase and ordering. **Intended behaviour changes (the point, not regressions):** non-ride post-session days advance to `post_training`, and evening leads with Tonight as a real phase — the pinned section/evening tests were updated to document this; per-section renders are unchanged. **Boundaries kept:** no verdict/fan/analysis-engine change, no new coaching logic, **no migration**, 45–47 wiring untouched, and `loopState` is optional in the shared schema so pre-48 cached payloads still parse. **Verification (local, all green):** backend ruff + `ruff format --check` clean, mypy **92 files** clean; 34 pure `test_daily_loop_state.py` cases pass; touched `test_daily_loop.py` (incl. a new DB-backed consolidation block-boundary test + a non-flaky `loopState`-shape assertion) runs 34 passed / 7 skipped locally (DB cases skip without Postgres, run in CI); shared typecheck + 10 tests; web lint 0 errors (5 pre-existing Fast-Refresh warnings), full web vitest **89 passed / 19 files** (new `useDailyPhase.test.ts` + rewritten `homeSections.test.ts`), `tsc` clean, and the web build is clean **under Node 20** — local Node 18 trips a **pre-existing** `vite-plugin-pwa`/`workbox-build` dynamic-require failure (reproduced with the batch stashed), unrelated to this change. PR #68 CI then went green across backend pytest/ruff/mypy, Alembic migration check, security audit, web build, and the Vercel preview; squash-merged to `main` as `d9060a1`. **Production verified on merge SHA `d9060a1`:** Railway and Vercel same-origin `/api/v1/health` both returned `sha=d9060a1ecefd1efb829d5174d36565a8343238b5`, web `/` returned 200, and `GET /api/v1/daily-loop` returned 401 unauthenticated both direct and via the Vercel rewrite (non-mutating auth-gated smoke; the app booted cleanly with the new `loopState` serializer). **Next step:** the passive-first plan (Batches 45–48) is **complete** — `docs/phase-batches.md` has no remaining unshipped batch, and the daily-flow redesign + v1–v3 roadmaps are all shipped. **Deferred follow-up (no ticket):** the orchestration seam is available but the scheduler doesn't consume it yet — Batches 45–47's push/projection/block wiring can adopt `describe_loop_state` opportunistically when next touched (the scope call at `/batch-start`, DECISIONS #118).

**Also 2026-07-03: Home & navigation UX read → Batches 49–51 specced (design docs + ledger, not started).** A world-class UI/UX pass over the shipped app with Craig, against the two-loop intent (sleep→training daily, block→block per block) on "effortless, not empty", now that the app is push-first (Batch 45). **Finding:** the bones are strong — three-tabs-plus-More, verdict-first Home, and collapse-not-remove (Batch 37) are all kept — but two structural gaps remain: (1) the layout is training-forward, so the *sleep* half of the daily loop (last night, tonight's projection, the Batch 27 bedroom-fan autopilot) has **no nav presence** (reachable only via Home detail-links) while `Trends` holds a primary slot; and (2) Home hasn't caught up to push-first — the one expanded section is chosen by *time/phase*, so an actionable item (a pending coach adjustment, an unlogged ride check-in) can sit collapsed and invisible in a non-primary section, and collapsed summaries don't signal that they need a tap. Plus minor "More"-menu jargon for a non-technical daily user. **Three frontend-only, no-migration batches close them:** **49 — Navigation & IA refactor + Sleep hub** (🟢 Mid, ships first: primary tabs → Home / Week / Sleep, a `/sleep` hub composing the existing sleep/bedroom surfaces with `/bedroom` absorbed, `Trends` demoted, "More" re-tiered + de-jargoned; `docs/designs/navigation-sleep-hub.md`); **50 — Action-first Home** (🔴 High: a deterministic `nextAction` resolver drives a "Next" strip + overrides the phase→primary expansion so actions surface regardless of time, with state-signalling collapsed summaries and the duplicated verdict badge dropped; `docs/designs/action-first-home.md`); **51 — Desktop two-column dashboard** (🟢 Mid, **optional/last**: layout-only polish; `docs/designs/desktop-dashboard-layout.md`). Sequence 49 → 50 → 51 (51 deferrable). Decision numbers assigned at `/batch-start` (next free **#119**); ledger: `docs/phase-batches.md` → "Post-roadmap — Home & navigation UX batch plan". **This supersedes the Batch 48 block's "passive-first plan complete / no remaining unshipped batch"** — the frontier is now the Home/nav UX plan. **Batch 45 — Proactive push + fan-reconciled nudges — SHIPPED (PR #65, squash `0d6ad9f`), prod-verified.** Backend-only, no migration (DECISIONS #115; spec `docs/designs/proactive-push-fan-reconciled.md`). First batch of the passive-first plan — turns the app **push-first** and stops the evening thermal nudges contradicting the Batch 27 fan autopilot. **45.1/45.2 proactive push:** the two highest-value outputs were generated silently — `run_morning_weather_sync` stored the Green/Amber/Red verdict and the hourly `run_garmin_activity_poll` stored each per-session read, but neither pushed; only the static 20:00 nudge + thermal/stale alerts reached Mark. Now `NudgeAlertService` gains `push_morning_verdict` (title `Today: {Green|Amber|Red}` + the verdict's first reason, deep-links `/`) and `push_workout_analysis` (per ride/strength/flexibility/walk, deep-links `/`), both reusing the existing `_send_once` → `send_notification` boundary + the `analyses`-tag idempotency so a verdict pushes **once per (profile, day)** (tag `verdict-{date}`, 09:30-backstop + regeneration safe) and an analysis pushes **once per activity** (tag `analysis-{activity_id}`, so a newer check-in / `PROMPT_VERSION` bump never re-pushes). Breathwork has no per-session analysis (#112) so nothing to push. New audit `analysis_type`s `verdict_push`/`analysis_push` follow the `evening_nudge` audit precedent — **never surfaced** on `/api/v1/daily-loop` or in reviews/handover (every `Analysis` reader filters by type). Each push is wrapped so a failure never blocks the generating pass; the verdict push self-commits, the post-workout pushes land in the poll's trailing commit (helper `_push_new_analyses`). **45.3 fan-reconciled thermal nudges:** `evaluate_thermal_alert` now takes a `FanReconcileState` (from `Profile.fan_auto_enabled` + the latest `fan_state_readings` tick); when the autopilot is armed the manual pre-cool/seal nudges are **suppressed** (the fan manages the room overnight) and a single **"check the fan"** push (deep-links `/bedroom`) is escalated **only** while the room is warm (≥ `ON_THRESHOLD_C` 19.5 °C) **and** the fan can't cope — latest action `unreachable`/`no_data`, or ≥ 20 °C while the fan is at `MAX_SPEED`; a comfortable room is silent even if the fan is unreachable (nothing to physically act on). Autopilot **off** keeps the pre-Batch-45 manual protocol nudges unchanged. **Quiet-hours honesty:** a quiet-hours-suppressed push still records its `_send_once` audit row (send returns 0 but the row is written), so it is not retried next poll. **Boundaries kept:** no migration, no coaching-logic change — the `fan_control.py` decision logic/thresholds, the Green/Amber/Red verdict, and recovery isolation (#49/#80) are untouched; no frontend/shared change (pushes ride the existing web-push path; a per-category Settings toggle is a deferred nice-to-have). **Verification (local):** backend ruff + `ruff format --check` clean, mypy **89 files** clean, full pytest **431 passed / 144 skipped** (the 3 DB-backed push/fan-read tests run in CI — no local Postgres on this Mac; fixed by seeding a real `Activity` row and keying the analyses off its id (mirroring `test_post_strength_analysis.py`), pushed as a follow-up commit, then CI went green across backend pytest/ruff/mypy, Alembic migration check, security audit, web build, and the Vercel preview. **Production verified on merge SHA `0d6ad9f`:** Railway `/api/v1/health` and Vercel same-origin `/api/v1/health` both returned `sha=0d6ad9fb…`, web `/` returned 200, and `GET /api/v1/daily-loop` returned 401 unauthenticated both direct and via the Vercel rewrite (non-mutating auth-gated smoke; the batch adds no new endpoint — the push logic runs in the scheduler). **First-live-use:** pushes only land on devices with an active `PushSubscription` + VAPID configured in Railway; confirm Mark's device is subscribed so the verdict/analysis pushes actually arrive. **Next step:** Batches **46** (evening sleep projection) + **47** (block-to-block progression) are the next unshipped batches and can proceed in parallel — 46 closes the daily loop back to sleep, 47 builds the per-block coupling; **Batch 44 — Interval-resolved ride analysis — SHIPPED (PR #63, squash `432e6b4`), prod-verified.** Backend-focused + optional frontend interval table, no migration (DECISIONS #114; spec `docs/designs/interval-resolved-ride-analysis.md`). Fixes the accuracy bug Mark named — the post-ride read judged a structured ride by its **blended whole-ride average power** (or its name), so warm-up + recovery valleys + cool-down dragged the average below the work band and mis-rated a clean session. Now the executed per-second trace (`ActivityTimeSeries`, #93) is segmented on the **planned IR's** interval boundaries (`build_structured_workout_ir`, Batch 12.1 — no new Garmin call) and each **work** interval is graded on its own %FTP target; warm-up/recovery/cool-down power is described, never graded. New pure `services/ride_intervals.py` (`segment_ride_intervals` + `classify_roles` + `summarize_execution` + a shared `power_zone` now reused by the zone histogram) computes per-interval NP (30 s rolling, mean below the window) / %FTP / zone / `adherence` (`on`/`over`/`under`, ±5%-FTP tolerance) / `fade` (first-third vs last-third power) / `hrDriftPct`. `assemble_context_packet` now carries `plannedWorkoutIr` + `intervals` + an `execution` summary, **keeps** `activity.avgPowerWatts` + `timeSeriesSummary` but relabels them as context; the `SYSTEM_PROMPT` + `outputRules` grade on the work intervals and forbid treating the whole-ride average as under-performance; `PROMPT_VERSION` bumped to `post-workout-analysis-v2-2026-07-03`, and a new `_analysis_is_current` makes the hourly poll + backfill regenerate any analysis predating the live prompt. **Free/outdoor rides** (no planned IR) degrade to the current whole-ride + zone-histogram read (no regression). Optional 44.6 frontend: the daily-loop serializer surfaces `intervals`/`execution`, a typed `rideIntervalSchema` parses them, and a compact "Interval execution" table under the post-ride card grades the work intervals only (renders nothing for a free ride). **Recovery isolation preserved (#49/#80):** narrative + grading only — the recovery decision and Green/Amber/Red are untouched; idempotent; boundary fakeable. **Five `/batch-start` calls settled (DECISIONS #114):** IR-alignment over the trace (not Garmin splits); free-ride fallback; fade = power-fade **plus** a descriptive HR-drift signal (richer option); no numeric rating; backfill recent structured rides only via `python -m src.ride_analysis_backfill --since YYYY-MM-DD [--commit]`. **Verification (local):** backend ruff + `ruff format --check` + mypy (89 files) clean, full pytest **421 passed / 141 skipped** (the new DB-backed packet cases run in CI — no local Postgres on this Mac; pure `test_ride_intervals` has 11 cases + the pure `_planned_ride_ir` selector test); shared 10 tests; web lint 0 errors + **76 vitest** (incl. 2 new interval-table tests) + vite build clean. PR #63 CI green across backend pytest/ruff/mypy, Alembic migration check, security audit, web build, and Vercel preview; production verified on merge SHA `432e6b4`: Railway + Vercel same-origin `/api/v1/health` both returned `sha=432e6b4…`, web `/` returned 200, and `GET /api/v1/daily-loop` returned 401 unauthenticated direct and via Vercel. **First-live-use:** the interval-resolved read only applies to structured rides that have both a planned IR and a per-second trace; run `python -m src.ride_analysis_backfill --since 2026-06-01` (dry-run) then `--commit` to regenerate recent structured rides through the new packet — the `PROMPT_VERSION` bump also means the next hourly poll auto-regenerates recent rides. **Next step:** `docs/phase-batches.md` has no remaining unshipped batch (the daily-flow redesign ledger through Batch 44 is complete); deferred follow-ups from the spec — Garmin ground-truth splits (would also unlock interval structure for free/outdoor rides), a concision/density pass on the read, and a VO2max trend surface — are tracked in `docs/designs/interval-resolved-ride-analysis.md` for a future batch.

**Also 2026-07-03: passive-first loop reassessment → Batches 45–48 specced (design docs + ledger, not started).** Re-read the app with Craig against Mark's refined user story — two nested feedback loops (**last night's sleep → today's training**, daily; a **completed multi-week block → the next block**, per block) on an **"effortless, not empty"** principle: the app does the work and reaches out, while the rich data stays browsable (Mark enjoys it). **Finding:** the structure is sound and most of the loop is already built — the wake-triggered morning verdict → sleep-adjusted plan (`executable_coaching`), per-session reads for all five modalities (ride/strength/flexibility/walk + breathwork brief), and the real-world actuation Mark wants (the **Batch 27 Dreo fan autopilot already drives the bedroom overnight**) — so these are **connective tweaks, not a rebuild.** **Four batches close the gaps:** **45 — Proactive push + fan-reconciled nudges** (🔴 High, smallest/highest-impact: the morning verdict + every post-workout read are generated but **never pushed** — only the static 20:00 nudge + thermal/stale alerts push — and the evening thermal nudges still tell Mark to hand-cool a room the fan is managing;
